I know a lot of people say Ned should've won, but idk if I agree. Sure you can blame it on his body type, though I don't think that's the actual factor in this. To me at least, I prefer Eugene's because that's more my style, I really liked the cloak/cape thing with the hood, it really gave the dress a wow factor. While Ned used a lot of time to make the corset, like punching eyelets, etc (which is hard, I hit in 128 eyelets by hand, it's really not easy and can be very time consuming), in the long run, Eugene's was more reliable, I suppose you could say. At least that is how I look at it. Using tape won't hold long in comparison to a good seam. The hem would also probably tear quickly as he hadn't done anything with it. While it's a part of the look, it'll be easier to tear. For that part it could've been a good idea to use glue or something similar as in that way the loose threads would stay where they were without ripping everything else with it.  It's not always the clothing with the most effort wins because it can end up looking unfinished and Ned's dress kind of looked like that to me. But I was for certain it'd either come in 1st or 2nd, same with Eugene while I knew the two others would come last.  But all four of em did great as they had little time and whatnot to do this. I've sewn and designed clothes for a few years and even I would've struggled making something in just a few hours from scratch.

(I finally feel qualified to make big judgments on one of these whoo) as a regular cosplay contest judge and someone who has been cosplaying before I knew there was a word for it (about 10 years now give or take), Here's my thoughts:  I think I'd probably argue and push for Ned's dress for like 20+ minutes (as I'm sure they probably spent a good amount of their time arguing on this since I've had to do the same).   I'm not sure how intentional Eugene's folds and all were and how pre-planned they ended up, but I think that it's a lot easier to mess around and end up on Eugene's result than to mess around and end up on Ned's.   I also think that Eugene played it a little safe with a single fabric as mentioned, while Ned not only messed with 3 different fabrics, but also different patterns which can go really wrong if you put patterns together incorrectly.    And in my experience, sometimes you also have to take context of the creator into question, if two people are equal you have to look at if the person has pushed their limits at all with the creation, if they learned or grew, etc. Eugene is always trying new crazy styles, meanwhile you can really see how Ned was trying something new and exciting with his.   Over all, I think they were both beautiful and fun, but in all of my main judgments on the garments, I would have put Ned barely above Eugene in most every aspect.   BUT I would give it 20 minutes of aggressively pushing for Ned until I begin to negotiate compromise/settling on my thoughts. If the other judges brought up enough strong points and whatnot, I would be open to eventually conceding on the fact. almost every time, the lineups at my con end up differently than I initially push, and that's why I'm not going to say Ned won in my book, because I think arguing with these guys for a long while could convince me away from Ned.   TL;DR: As a cosplay judge, I believe Ned deserved the win, BUT if my fellow judges argued and pushed me enough I could be convinced to give up my say to Eugene after like half an hour of arguing with fellow judges.

I actually disagree with the majority of the comments here. In my opinion Ned has the lesser dress, and I'd like to explain my reasoning  Shape: Ned's dress had less shape. Yes, you can account for part of that with figure differences, but bear in mind that Ned attempted to make a corset and so should have been able to achieve more shape. In fact you can even see in the back where his lacing was gaping because he didn't have enough boning to give him structure  Waist: that skirt waist location was really poorly chosen. It throws the whole balance of the garment off, which is really disappointing because of how much effort he put in. And using the taped on stud belt didn't help, in my opinion. The look would have pulled together better with a draped and angled belt  Neckline: he had a completely straight neck, no shaping, it was just folded over and taped down. He could have given it the sweetheart neckline he had in his design image!  Too many textures: I might be disagreeing with the majority here but I felt that Ned had too many textures in his. He overdid the writing and it just made it too busy. If he'd used a fabric that had a base texture it would have worked better, or perhaps done a black lace overlay for texture. But the writing didn't add to it  Raw edges: the skirt didn't look intentionally designed with the raw edges, it just looked more slapdash. I think the raw look would have gone better if he'd used a more jagged cut. Or if he'd gone through with the pleats!   Whereas for Eugene's  Colour: I actually liked the monochromatic look, the only thing I would have changed would be to use a fabric with more texture, or maybe even decorative embroidery to highlight areas  Shape: Eugene's fit him better and that's a fact. Yes, like 1 or 2 tiny spots didn't sit perfectly, but he actually had his waist sit at the right height, and the draping on the shoulders was well executed. Same with his neckline, the tapering suited his shape better  Texture: I disagreed with the judges when they said Eugene's needed more texture, and it clearly shows the judges weren't considering a historical fashion basis which is what Eugene was going for in his design. I think embellishments would have detracted from the look. Maybe some pearls or broaches, but nothing more in my opinion  Construction: Eugene's the only one who didn't cop out and use adhesives  Eugene had the better overall garment. Ned did AMAZING and I would love to see Ned remake his piece with more time, with help from a seamstress, and putting it on different models. It would look STUNNING! But for the purposes of this competition Eugene did pull ahead when push came to shove, and that's the truth  But Ned PLEASE DON'T BE DISCOURAGED! That was a really close call and honestly just a few tweaks would have really pulled it over the line. I actually think Ned could really have a solid crack at fashion design, and I would love to see a video of him and Eugene designing a series of outfits together! They both have developed keen eyes for it

Easiest way to make a dress. Measure your bust, then under your arm pits, than waist should be level with your belly button then wides part of your hips about 9 inches down from your waist. Then measure from the sticky out bit at the base if your neck to your waist. Divide the waist by 4 and your bust by 4. Use those measurements to create 4 panels for a bodice. Use the divided waist measurements for the top of the skirt, and times the divided waist by 8 to create a skirt panel. Measure from your waist to however long you want the skirt. Cut 4 of those panels. Leave a seam allowance, stitch them all together. Use 2 strips of fabric to do straps for your dress and voilÃ  one dress
